# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of Django migration squashing compliance and created the answer.json file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Django Migration Squashing Implementation

I identified **9 key Python source files** implementing migration squashing compliance:

### Core Components:

1. **Squash Migration Generator** - `django/core/management/commands/squashmigrations.py`
   - Generates new squashed migrations with the `replaces` attribute
   - Handles dependency collection and operation optimization

2. **Replaced-Migrations Tracking** - `django/db/migrations/loader.py`
   - Maintains a replacements dictionary tracking all squashed migrations
   - The `replace_migration()` method processes replacements with circular dependency detection
   - `_resolve_replaced_migration_keys()` recursively resolves transitive replacements

3. **Dependency Graph Validation** - `django/db/migrations/graph.py`
   - `remove_replaced_nodes()` - removes replaced migrations and remaps dependencies
   - `remove_replacement_node()` - handles partially applied squashed migrations
   - `validate_consistency()` - ensures graph integrity

4. **Squash Completeness Check** - `django/db/migrations/executor.py`
   - `check_replacements()` method marks squashed migrations as applied when all replacements are applied
   - Uses `all_replaced_applied()` for recursive validation

### Supporting Files:
- `migration.py` - Migration base class with `replaces` attribute
- `optimizer.py` - Optimizes operation sequences
- `exceptions.py` - Exception types for validation errors
- `writer.py` - Serializes migration files
- `recorder.py` - Records applied migrations

  "content": "{\"content\":\"1: from functools import total_ordering\\n2: \\n3: from django.db.migrations.state import ProjectState\\n4: from django.utils.datastructures import OrderedSet\\n5: \\n6: from .exceptions import CircularDependencyError, NodeNotFoundError\\n7: \\n8: \\n9: @total_ordering\\n10: class Node:\\n11:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n12:     A single node in the migration graph. There are\\n69:     no implicit dependencies between numbered migrations - the numbering is\\n70:     merely a convention to aid file listing. Every new numbered migration\\n71:     has a declared dependency to the previous number, meaning that VCS\\n72:     branch merges can be detected and resolved.\\n73: \\n74:     Migrations files can be marked as replacing another set of migrations -\\n75:     this is to support the \\\"squash\\\" feature. The graph handler isn't\\n76:     responsible for these; instead, the code to load them in here should\\n77:     examine the migration files and if the replaced migrations are all either\\n78:     unapplied or not present, it should ignore the replaced ones, load in just\\n79:     the replacing migration, and repoint any dependencies that pointed to the\\n80:     replaced migrations to point to the replacing one.\\n81: \\n82:     A node should be a tuple: (app_path, migration_name). The tree\\n83:     special-cases things within an app - namely, root nodes and leaf nodes\\n84:     ignore dependencies to other apps.\\n85:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n86: \\n87:     def __init__(self):\\n88:         self.node_map = {}\\n89:         self.nodes = {}\\n90: \\n91:     def add_node(self, key, migration):\\n92:         assert key not in self.node_map\\n93:         node = Node(key)\\n94:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n95:         self.nodes[key] = migration\\n96: \\n97:     def add_dummy_node(self, key, origin, error_message):\\n98:         node = DummyNode(key, origin, error_message)\\n99:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n100:         self.nodes[key] = None\\n101: \\n102:     def add_dependency(self, migration, child, parent, skip_validation=False):\\n103:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n104:         This may create dummy nodes if they don't yet exist. The _resolve_replaced_migration_keys() method recursively resolves the actual replaced migrations even when multiple squashed migrations reference each other.\\n\\n3. **Dependency Graph Validation After Squashing** (django/db/migrations/graph.py): The MigrationGraph class provides two critical methods for handling squashed migrations:\\n   - validate_consistency(): Ensures no dummy nodes remain in the graph, which would indicate missing dependencies\\n\\n4. **Squash Completeness Check** (django/db/migrations/executor.py): The check_replacements() method in MigrationExecutor marks replacement migrations as applied when all their replaced migrations are applied, using the loader's all_replaced_applied() method which recursively checks if all replaced migrations (including those transitively replaced by other squashed migrations) have been applied in the database.\\n\\nAdditional supporting files include:\\n- django/db/migrations/migration.py: Defines the Migration base class with the `replaces` attribute\\n- django/db/migrations/optimizer.py: Optimizes operations sequences during squash generation\\n- django/db/migrations/exceptions.py: Defines exception types (NodeNotFoundError, InconsistentMigrationHistory, CircularDependencyError) used for validation\\n- django/db/migrations/writer.py: Serializes and writes migration files\\n- django/db/migrations/recorder.py: Records applied migration status in the database\\n\\nThe entire flow ensures that squashed migrations can coexist with their replaced migrations, Django intelligently switches between them based on migration history state, and circular dependency scenarios are detected and prevented.\"\n}\n",

compliance is implemented across multiple Python source files in the django/django repository. The architecture consists of four main components:\\n\\n1. **Squash Migration Generator** (django/core/management/commands/squashmigrations.py): The Command class's handle() method generates new squashed migrations by collecting operations and dependencies from a range of migrations, optimizing them using MigrationOptimizer, and creating a new Migration instance with the `replaces` attribute set to the list of replaced migrations.\\n\\n2. **Replaced-Migrations Tracking** (django/db/migrations/loader.py): The MigrationLoader class maintains a replacements dictionary during build_graph() that tracks all migrations marked with non-empty `replaces` attributes. The replace_migration() method processes these tracked migrations and validates for circular dependencies, raising CommandError if a cyclical squash replacement is detected. The _resolve_replaced_migration_keys() method recursively resolves the actual replaced migrations even when multiple squashed migrations reference each other.\\n\\n3. **Dependency Graph Validation After Squashing** (django/db/migrations/graph.py): The MigrationGraph class provides two critical methods for handling squashed migrations:\\n   - remove_replaced_nodes(): Removes replaced migration nodes from the graph and remaps dependencies pointing to them to the replacement node\\n   - remove_replacement_node(): The inverse operation that removes a replacement node and remaps its dependents to the replaced nodes (used when a squashed migration is partially applied)\\n   - validate_consistency(): Ensures no dummy nodes remain in the graph, which would indicate missing dependencies\\n\\n4. **Squash Completeness Check** (django/db/migrations/executor.py): The check_replacements() method in MigrationExecutor marks replacement migrations as applied when all their replaced migrations are applied, using the loader's all_replaced_applied() method which recursively checks if all replaced migrations (including those transitively replaced by other squashed migrations) have been applied in the database.\\n\\nAdditional supporting files include:\\n- django/db/migrations/migration.py: Defines the Migration base class with the `replaces` attribute\\n- django/db/migrations/optimizer.py: Optimizes operations sequences during squash generation\\n- django/db/migrations/exceptions.py: Defines exception types (NodeNotFoundError, InconsistentMigrationHistory, CircularDependencyError) used for validation\\n- django/db/migrations/writer.py: Serializes and writes migration files\\n- django/db/migrations/recorder.py: Records applied migration status in the database\\n\\nThe entire flow ensures that squashed migrations can coexist with their replaced migrations, Django intelligently switches between them based on migration history state, and circular dependency scenarios are detected and prevented.\"\n}\n",
